The respondent have throughout complied with the terms of the agreement and made every effort to perform the agreement by trying to pay the balance amount of the purchase price which was not accepted without objection. It was submitted that legitimate expectation has been developed when the possession of the Mill was transferred in accordance with the agreement. After the appellants restrained the petitioner from carrying on any activity in relation to the Mill, the respondents received the 1st and 2nd installments from the respondent under the agreement and therefore, the respondents further legitimately expressed that the restraining order of the appellants has no legal force in the eye of law. However,</span></span> <span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">although the appellants accepted the 1st and 2<sup>nd</sup> installment money from the respondent under the Agreement, the appellant did not allow the respondents to resume their activity in relation to the Mill. The appellants most illegally, unfairly and with ulterior motive refused to accept the remaining installments from the respondents and take necessary steps to </span></span><span class="FontStyle19"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Narrow'; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">execute and register sale deed in accordance </span></span><span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">with the terms and conditions of the Agreement </span></span><span class="FontStyle19"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Arial Narrow'; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">although more than</span></span> <span class="FontStyle11"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Book Antiqua';">60% of the purchase price has already been paid, there has been an utter violation of the principle of promissory estoppel. It was further submitted that the appellants entered into the agreement with the respondent in exercise of its statutory power granted vide Memo No.MOT/Admn/B-13/2001/dated 13.11.2003 and as such, violation of the terms of the agreement is illegal. Lastly it was submitted that the writ is quite maintainable and the Government cannot go beyond its promise made in accordance with law and the liquidator is the proper authority to deal with the matter and the respondent is the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> purchaser with value of the Mill in question. </span></span></p><p class="Style1" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">We have considered the submissions of the learned Attorney General for the appellants and the learned Counsel appearing for the respondents and perused the impugned judgement of the High Court Division and other connected papers on record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">It appears from the impugned judgement that the Government invited international tender on four occasions, but the Mill could not be sold. Upon decision for winding up of the Mill, the Official Liquidator writ-respondent No.2 was appointed to take all actions required to be taken and all responsibilities required to be discharged in this regard.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">From the record we find that the writ-petitioner, vide different applications made to respondent No.2, expressed its intention of purchasing the Mill. However, we do not find that writ-respondent No.2 was invested with any power to sell the Mill other than by tender. We find nothing on record to suggest that the Mill could be sold by mutual agreement. The powers of the Liquidator are enumerated in his terms of reference. But these do not include selling the property under liquidation by any means other than through tender. Moreover we note that the Liquidation Cell had already been abolished in the meantime and was not in existence at the time of the Deed of Agreement. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The fact that the writ-petitioner was in default in paying his instalments in accordance with the terms of the Agreement is a secondary issue. The primary question that requires an answer is the validity of entering into an agreement for sale at the behest of the Minister of the concerned Ministry. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The High Court Division observed that debarring the writ-petitioner from carrying on any activity relating to the Mills in spite of the instalments received from the writ-petitioner and the respondents’ deliberate failure to receive instalment for the balance amount from the writ-petitioner and execute and register necessary sale deed in favour of the writ-petitioner in compliance with the terms and of the Agreement have clearly infringed the writ-petitioner’s fundamental right to property guaranteed and protected under article 42 of part III of the Constitution of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh although the writ-petitioner has throughout complied with the terms of the Agreement and had made every effort to perform his part of the obligation in terms of the Agreement by trying to pay the balance amount of the purchase price which was not accepted by the respondents. However, we are of the view that the Agreement entered into by the writ-petitioner had no legal basis. Hence, there was no question of any right accruing in favour of the writ-petitioner. We <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">say so, firstly because the Liquidator apparently</span> did not exist at that time. Secondly, his power with regard to the Mill was only to the extent of selling the same through tender and not by any agreement. Every part of the transaction that followed, including payment and acceptance of instalments was without lawful authority.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Before concluding, we should also deal with the matter as to whether the contract entered into by the respondents with the Government of Bangladesh is a sovereign contract or merely a commercial contract. In this regard we may refer to the decision in the case of <strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Sharping Matshajibi Samabaya Samity Ltd Vs. Bangladesh and ors.</em></strong> reported in 39 DLR(AD)85. In that case Badrul Haider Chowdhury, J as his Lordship was then, observed as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 9pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>“Modern Government has multifarious activities. Some of its functions are Governmental function while exercising sovereign power and again some of the functions can be described as trading function.” His Lordship went on to say that “when the Government grants lease, privilege, settlement, etc., the Government acts and discharges sovereign function ‘performing function in connection with affairs of the republic or the local authority”. His Lordship observed that the Government acts in these affairs in pursuance of some statutory power and any such contract when rooted in statute, the Government discharges its sovereign functions. In the instant case the learned Advocate for the respondents submitted that the sale of the property having taken place in furtherance of authority provided in President’s Order 27 of 1972, the contract for sale was a statutory contract. In this context we may profitably refer to the decision in the case of <strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Bangladesh Power Development Board and others vs Md. Asaduzzaman Sikder</em></strong> reported in <strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">9 BLC (AD) 1,</em></strong> where it was argued that the contract entered into by virtue of section 17(2)(a) of P.O.59 of 1972 rendered it as a statutory contract. However, their Lordships expressed the opinion that “The contract which the Board may enter into as per the aforesaid provision is an enacting or enabling provision in the execution of its works, like the work as was undertaken upon entering into contract with the respondent. The contract that was entered into by the appellants with the respondent was not in terms of statutory provision or in exercise of statutory power but the contract so entered into was an ordinary commercial contract or contract of general nature or, in other words, a pure and simple contract.” Their Lordships concluded that the relief sought for and granted by the High Court Division was not legally available to the respondent. With respect, we are of the view that in the facts of the instant case the contract entered into by the Official Liquidator is not a statutory contract, apart from the fact that, as we have noted above, the post of the liquidator had been abolished and in any event the liquidator was authorised to sell the property in question through tender.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In the later case of <strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Superintendent Engineer, RHD Sylhet and others v. Md. Eunus and Brothers (Pvt.) Ltd. </em></strong>reported <strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">in 31 BLD (AD) 1</em></strong> the decision of this Division reported in <strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">9 BLC (AD)1</em></strong>, noted earlier, was considered and six conditions were formulated, which would permit entertaining an application within the writ jurisdiction in case of breach of contract. These were as follows: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.75in; text-indent: -0.25in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em><!--[endif]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">the contract is entered into by the Government in the capacity as sovereign;</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.75in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em><!--[endif]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">where contractual obligation sought to be enforced in writ jurisdiction arises out of statutory <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">duty or sovereign obligation or public</span> function of a public authority;</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.75in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em><!--[endif]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">where contract is entered into in exercise of an enacting power conferred by a statute that by itself does not render the contract a statutory contract, but ‘if ent<span style="color: #000000;">ering into a contract containing prescribed terms and conditions is a must under the statute then that contract becomes a statutory contract. If a contract incorporates certain terms and conditions in it which are statutory then the said contract to that extent is statutory’; </span></span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.75in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em><!--[endif]--></span><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="color: #000000;">where a statute may expressly or im</span>pliedly confer power on a statutory body to enter into contracts in order to enable it to discharge its functions and the contract so entered by the statutory power then merely because one of the parties to the contract is statutory or public body such contract is not a statutory contract;</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.75in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(e)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em><!--[endif]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">when contract is entered into by a public authority invested with the statutory power, in case of breach thereof relief in writ jurisdiction may be sought as against such on the plea that the contract was entered into by the public authority invested with a statutory power; </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.75in; text-indent: -0.25in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(f)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></em><!--[endif]--><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">where the contract has been entered into in exercise of statutory power by a statutory authority in terms of the statutory provisions and then breach thereof gives right to the aggrieved party to invoke writ jurisdiction because the relief sought is against breach of statutory obligation.” </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In the aforesaid case tender had been issued by the Roads and Highways Department for the construction of a bridge. The writ-petitioner challenged the Department due to the fact that their bid was not successful. Before this Division it was argued that the writ petition involved a commercial contract and hence, the High Court Division was wrong in holding the writ petition maintainable. Upon referring to the six conditions noted above, it was held that the contract does not fulfill any of the requirements to make the same statutory contract or contract entered into by the Government in the capacity as sovereign. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In the light of the above discussion we find that the contract in question having been entered into by the official liquidator was not a sovereign contract and hence it was not amenable to the writ jurisdiction.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Considering all aspects of the case, the appeal is allowed and the judgement and order of the High Court Division is set aside. There will be no order as to costs.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue_May____19(1)/Issue__May_19__C.%20A.%20181%20of%2016__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali,%20J___AD___2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">CIVIL APPEAL No.</span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> 181 OF 2016</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgment and order dated 15th of June, 2015 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.10820 of 2014)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
760	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Islami Bank Bangladesh Ltd. Vs.  Al-Mozadded Shipping Lines, (Ahmed Sohel, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> First Miscellaneous Appeal No. 105 of 2012  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  S. M. Emdadul Hoque, J And Ahmed Sohel, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Ahsanul Karim, Advocate with Mr. Khairul Alam Chowdhury, Advocate Mr. Md. Kabir Iqbal Hossain, Advocate Ms. Farzana Khan, Advocate  ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Islami Bank Bangladesh Limited and others  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Al-Mozadded Shipping Lines Co. and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Artha Rin Adalat Ain </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 181px;" width="554"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 245.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">S. M. Emdadul Hoque, J</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">And</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Ahmed Sohel, J</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">16.10.2018</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 44.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue_May____19(1)/Issue%20__May__19__F.M.A.%20105%20of%2014__Ahmed%20Sohel__2.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 220.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Islami Bank Bangladesh Limited and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . Petitioners</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Al-Mozadded Shipping Lines Co. and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">. . . Opposite parties </span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; line-height: 120%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a name="_Hlk8417659" style="color: #000000;"></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 120%;">Artha Rin Adalat Ain </span></strong><a name="_Hlk8417647" style="color: #000000;"></a><span style="mso-bookmark: _Hlk8417659;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(VIII of 2003)</span></strong></span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 19 (2)(3)(4)</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Artha Rin Adalat Ain, 2003 gives a clear understanding that right after passing of the ex-parte decree or from the date of knowledge of the ex-parte decree if within 30 days as per sub-section (3) of section 19 by depositing 10% of the decreetal amount an application has been filed for restoration of the suit after setting –aside the ex-parte decree, the suit will be automatically restored in terms of section 19(4) of the Ain to its original file and number.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">An application for restoration of the suit after setting-aside ex-parte decree may be made within 30 days right after passing of the ex-parte decree or from the date of knowledge of the ex-parte decree. . . . (21 and 22)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Artha Rin Adalat Ain (VIII of 2003)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 19 (2)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">After pronouncement of ex-parte decree a legal right has been accrued in favour of the plaintiff (decree holder) and allowing of an application for setting aside the said decree, is curtailing the accrued right of the decree holder.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The plaintiff has got a right to be informed about hearing of the said application by proper notice and the Adalat after hearing both the parties shall decide the issue as to correctness of the defendants alleged date of knowledge in order to satisfy itself towards the compliance of Section 19(2) of the Ain.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>. . . </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(30 and 31)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Limitation Act (IX of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Sections 3 and 5</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">As per Section 3 of the Limitation Act, 1908, which confers a duty upon the Court to see as to whether the suit/application is filed within time or not even if the issue of limitation has not been pressed, the court is legally bound to see and decide such issue in disposing of the matter before it.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Where a time limit has been given to file an appeal, the provision of section 5 of limitation Act will not apply and the Artha Rin Adalat Ain 2003, being a special law, the provisions of Section 5 of the limitation Act will not apply and therefore the application for restoration shall be rejected outright.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">       </span>. . . </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(35 and 36)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Contract Act (IX of 1872)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 17</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">He who comes into equity must come with clean hands’. It operates to prevent any affirmative recovery for the person with ‘unclean hands’ no matters how unfairly, the persons adversary has treated him or her. The maxim is the basis of the clean hands doctrine. Its purpose is to protect the integrity of the Court.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It is to be borne in mind that fraud or suppression of fact and fair play cannot dwell together, one must exclude the other. The Court stands for fair play only and to get equitable relief the respondent must approach the Court with </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">clean hands. An act of fraud on Court is always</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> viewed seriously. In judicial proceedings, once fraud is proved, all advantages gained by playing fraud can be taken away. Suppression of any material fact/document amounts to a fraud upon the court.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">When facts are intentionally misrepresented or </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">where a false statement is made intentionally,</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> with the knowledge that it is false, with a view to deceive the other party, it is known as fraud. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">In the present case, it is clear that the respondents had knowledge of the ex-parte decree at least in the year of 2009, which is clearly suppression of facts and amounts to committing fraud upon the Court. It is crystal clear that the Adalat has committed wrong in passing the impugned order dated 16.01.2012 without deciding the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">question of limitation, which is a non speaking</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">order and erroneous and should be interfered</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;"> with as fraud has been committed upon the court. Thus we find merit in the Appeal.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                </span></span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(37, 41, 43 and 44)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bangladesh Development Bank Ltd </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Vs. </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judge Artha Rin Adalat, Jessore</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> and</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> others 66 DLR (HCD) 1; Pubali Bank Ltd </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Vs. </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bangladesh and others 66 DLR (HCD) 317;</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Maneka Gandhi </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Vs. </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Union of India AIR 1978</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(SC)</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">597;</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Zillur Rahman (Md) </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Vs. </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Md. Abdul Quiyum Sarker 18 BLC</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(AD) 258;</span></em></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Janata Insurance Company Ltd </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Vs. </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Commissioner, Customs, Excise and VAT, Dhaka and others 18 BLC (HCD) 562 and United India Insurance Co. Ltd </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Vs</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. Rajendra Singh and others AIR 2000 SC 1165 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Mr. Ahsanul Karim, Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Mr. Khairul Alam Chowdhury, Advocate</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Mr. Md. Kabir Iqbal Hossain, Advocate</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Ms. Farzana Khan, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">. . . For the Appellants.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Mr. Md. Reza-E-Murshed Kamal, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">. . . For the Respondents.</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 120%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span lang="X-NONE" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Ahmed Sohel, J:</span></u></strong> <span lang="X-NONE" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">This First Miscellaneous</span><span lang="X-NONE" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;"> Appeal filed by the appellant, Islami Bank Bangladesh Limited is directed against the impugned order No. 10 dated 06.01.2012, under Section 19(2) of the Artha Rin Adalat Ain, 2003, passed by the learned Judge Artha Rin Adalat No. 4, Dhaka in Miscellaneous <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Case No. 1 of 2012 arising out of Artha Rin Suit</span> No. 619 of 2008 allowing the Miscellaneous Case and thereby setting aside the ex-parte judgment and decree dated 22.03.2009 passed in Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="X-NONE" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="X-NONE" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Facts necessary for disposal of the Appeal, in short, is that the present appellants as plaintiffs filed Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008 in the Court of Artha Rin Adalat No. 4, Dhaka (hereinafter referred to as Adalat) against the respondents praying for a decree for recovery of outstanding loan of Taka 1,72,22461.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">The defendants of the Artha Rin Suit did not appear and contested the suit although summons were duly served upon them as per the report of the process server. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">The learned Judge, Artha Rin Adalat fixed the date on 22.03.2009 for ex-parte hearing of the Artha Rin Suit and on that date passed the ex-parte judgment and decree against the defendants which was drawn on 25.03.2009.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">In pursuant to the ex-parte decree the appellant as decree holder filed application for execution before the Artha Rin Adalat No. 4, Dhaka describing in the schedule both immovable property and cargo vessel to be sold in execution for realization of decreetal sum and was registered as Artha Jari Case No. 106 of 2009 and in due compliance of law got a certificate in its favour under Section 33(5) of Artha Rin Adalat Ain 2003. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">The decree holder Bank published auction notice in the ‘Daily Songram’ and ‘Dainik Amar Desh’ to sell the mortgaged property fixing 13.04.2011 as the date of Auction.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>The Auction took place on the above date after completing all the formalities, delivery of possession of the Auction sold properties including the cargo vessel was completed and the decree holder appellant Bank received the auction price in accordance with law. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">That on 11.01.2012 the present respondents, the defendants of Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008 filed a Miscellaneous case No. 1 of 2012, under Section 19(2) of the Artha Rin Adalat Ain 2003 before the Adalat Dhaka for setting aside the ex-parte judgment and decree dated 22.03.2009 (decree signed on 25.03.2009) and also prayed for restoration of the suit to its original file and number stating inter alia that summons were not served upon them properly and that they knew nothing about the suit as well as the decree until 01.01.2012. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">The respondents of the present First Miscellaneous Appeal No. 105 of 2012 without serving any summons or notice or any copy of the said application upon the appellant, (plaintiff of the Artha Rin Suit) the learned Judge, of the Artha Rin Adalat after hearing the defendant only, pleased to allow the Miscellaneous Case on 16.01.2012 by setting aside the ex-parte decree dated 22.03.2009 and restored the Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008 to its original file and number. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Being aggrieved by the aforesaid impugned order No. 10 dated 16.01.2012 of the Adalat, the plaintiffs as appellants preferred this Miscellaneous Appeal before this Court with an application for stay operation of the impugned order dated 16.01.2012 passed by the Artha Rin Adalat No. 4, Dhaka, upon which this Court by the order dated 27.02.2012 issued Rule and stayed all further proceedings of Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008 for 03(three) months and later on the said stay has been extended till disposal of the Rule. The Rule was registered as Civil Rule No. 164(F.M) of 2012. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Mr. Ahsanul Karim, the learned Advocate appearing with Mr. Khairul Alam Choudhury, Mr. Md. Kabir Iqbal Hossain and Ms. Farzana Khan, learned Advocates on behalf of the appellants at the very outset submits that the Artha Rin Adalat committed serious error in law in allowing the miscellaneous case in particular that the learned Judge of the Artha Rin Adalat failed to consider that no notice and copy of the application under Section 19(2) of the Ain was served upon the plaintiffs-appellants before taking up the said application for disposal. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He further submits that the learned Judge, failed to discuss as to how the defendant respondents came to the finding about the knowledge of the respondents about the ex-parte order dated 22.03.2009, decree signed on 25.03.2009 passed in Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008 without considering any evidence in respect of limitation. In this respect he has drawn out attention to Annexure- F of the application for stay filed by the appellant, from where it is found that the defendant-respondents were very much aware of the decree passed ex-parte in Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008 as far back as at least in 2009 as it is evident that an application under Section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure had been filed before the Hon’ble High Court Division in Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 19420 of 2009 (wherein the present respondents had annexed the ex-parte decree dated 22.03.2009 (decree signed on 25.03.2009) as Annexure-<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>E in their application under Section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure) which clearly proves that they were well aware of the said ex-parte decree at least in 2009. The respondents claim that they knew nothing about the suit as well as the decree until 01.01.2012 was not correct at all. Therefore, the date of knowledge is clearly more than 30(thirty) days before filing of the application under Section 19(2) of the Artha Rin Adalat 2003, which is hopelessly barred by special law of limitation laid down in Section 19 of the Artha Rin Adalat Ain, 2003. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He next submits that without ascertaining the question of limitation, the learned Judge, having satisfied himself of compliance of only one requirement of deposit of 10% of the decreetal amount erroneously allowed the Miscellaneous Case without satisfying himself that the said application was not indeed filed within 30 days from the date of knowledge of the defendant-respondents and as such the impugned order is not sustainable in the eye of law and required to be set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">In support of his submissions, he referred 02(two) decisions, Bangladesh Development Bank Ltd vs Judge Artha Rin Adalat, Jessore and others reported in 66 DLR (HCD) 1; and Pubali Bank Ltd vs Bangladesh and others reported in 66 DLR (HCD) 317.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Furthermore, he submits that the suppression of facts amounts to fraud upon the Court and fraud vitiates everything and he is not entitled to get any relief due to this suppression of facts. Accordingly, he prayed for allowing the Appeal. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">On the other hand, Mr. Md. Reza-E-Murshed Kamal, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the respondents by filing an affidavit-in-opposition and Counter Affidavit, contesting the Appeal and submits that the facts of the case of the respondent opposite parties No. 1 to 3 are that they never applied for any loan in the said Bank rather one Mahbubur Rahman a Bank staff misguided the respondent opposite parties and provoked them to apply for loan.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He next submits that the present respondents did not know about the judgment and decree passed by the 4<sup>th</sup> Artha Rin Adalat, Dhaka in Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008. The respondents came to know firstly from the Criminal Case No. 1089 of 2011 filed by the Bank in the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate Court, Dhaka under section 419/420/465/467/ 471/109 of the Penal Code. Wherein an application dated 01.01.2012 has been filed for ‘shown arrest’ the accused petitioner and in that application, the number of Artha Rin Execution Case No. 47 of 2011 has been written. Thereafter after knowing about the said ex-parte order passed in Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008, the present respondents filed a Miscellaneous Case No. 01 of 2012 before the Artha Rin Adalat No. 4, Dhaka under section 19(2) of the Artha Rin Adalat Ain, 2003 for restoration of the original Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008 and the same was allowed and restored the said suit. However the said suit is now stayed by the order of the Hon’ble High Court Division in Civil Rule No. 164(F.M) of 2012 filed by the appellants. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">He further submits that the Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008 is totally false, manufactured and the defendants No. 1 to 3 are not responsible for the outstanding dues as demanded by the plaintiffs bank and is not entitled to get any relief as prayed for and the order of stay passed by the Hon’ble High Court Division in this Civil Rule is liable to be vacated for the ends of justice.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">At the time of hearing, the learned Advocate for the respondents was confronted with the question of date of knowledge of the exparte decree dated 22.03.2009 in particular the application filed by the respondents under Section 561A of Code of Criminal Procedure i.e. regarding Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 19420 of 2009, wherein the respondents annexed the certified copy of the judgment of the ex-parte decree dated 22.03.2009 (decree signed on 25.03.2009) that the respondents had knowledge of the ex-parte decree at least in the year of 2009 and this suppression of fact, amounts to committing fraud upon the Court. In reply the learned Counsel for the respondents finding himself in difficult position to address the point confronted with and could not give any satisfactory reply to this point of suppression of facts rather admitted it. However, he finally submits that for the ends of justice, the respondents should be given a last chance to contest the suit. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">We have heard the learned Advocates of both the parties with profound attention, perused the impugned order of the Adalat and the papers and documents as available on the record and the decisions of our apex Court very carefully. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Now, for the convenience of understanding Section 19 of Artha Rin Adalat Ain, 2003 is quoted below:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 3.25pt 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">“</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">19z (1) j¡jm¡l öe¡e£l SeÉ d¡kÑ ®L¡e a¡¢l­M ¢hh¡c£ Bc¡m­a Ae¤f¢ÙÛa b¡¢L­m, ¢Lwh¡ j¡jm¡ öe¡e£l SeÉ Nªq£a qCh¡l fl X¡¢Lu¡ ¢hh¡c£­L Ef¢ÙÛa f¡Ju¡ e¡ ®N­m, Bc¡ma j¡jm¡ HLalg¡ p§­œ ¢eÇf¢š L¢l­hz</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 3.25pt 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">(2) ®L¡e j¡jm¡ HLalg¡ p§­œ ¢Xœ²£ qC­m, ¢hh¡c£ Eš² HLalg¡ ¢Xœ²£l a¡¢l­Ml Abh¡ X~š² HLalg¡ ¢Xœ²£ pÇf­LÑ AhNa qCh¡l 30(¢œn) ¢ch­pl j­dÉ, Ef-d¡l¡ (3) Hl ¢hd¡e p¡­f­r, Eš² HLalg¡ ¢Xœ²£ l­cl SeÉ clM¡Ù¹ L¢l­a f¡¢l­hez </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 3.25pt 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">(3) Ef-d¡l¡ (2) Hl ¢hd¡e Ae¤k¡u£ clM¡Ù¹ c¡¢M­ml ®r­œ ¢hh¡c£­L Eš² clM¡Ù¹ c¡¢M­ml a¡¢l­Ml flha£Ñ 15(f­el)¢ch­pl j­dÉ ¢Xœ²£L«a A­bÑl 10% Hl pjf¢lj¡e V¡L¡ h¡c£l c¡h£l ®pC f¢lj¡­el SeÉ ü£L«¢aül©f eNc pw¢nÔø B¢bÑL fË¢aù¡­e, Abh¡ S¡j¡eaül©f hÉ¡wL XÊ¡gV, ®f-AX¡l h¡ AeÉ ®L¡e fËL¡l eNc¡ue­k¡NÉ ¢h¢e­ju c¢mm (</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Negotiable Instrument</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">) BL¡­l S¡j¡ea ¢qp¡h Bc¡m­a Sj¡c¡e L¢l­a qC­hz </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 3.25pt 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">(4) Ef-d¡l¡ (3) Hl ¢hd¡ej­a ¢Xœ²£L«a A­bÑl 10% Hl pjf¢lj¡e V¡L¡ Sj¡c¡­el pw­N pw­N clM¡Ù¹¢V j”¤l qC­h, Hlalg¡ ¢Xœ²£ lc qC­h Hhw j¤m j¡jm¡ Eq¡l f§­hÑl eðl J e¢b­a f¤el¦‹£¢ha qC­h, Hhw Bc¡ma I j­jÑ HL¢V B­cn ¢m¢fhÜ L¢l­h, Hhw Aaxfl j¡jm¡¢V ®k fkÑ¡­u HLalg¡ ¢eÇf¢š qCu¡¢Rm, I fkÑ¡­ul AhÉh¢qa f§hÑha£Ñ fk¡Ñu qC­a f¢lQ¡¢ma qC­hz </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 3.25pt 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">(5) ¢hh¡c£ Ef-d¡l¡ (3) ¢hd¡ej­a ¢Xœ²£L«a A­bÑl 10% Hl pjf¢lj¡e V¡L¡ h¡c£l c¡h£l ®pC f¢lj¡­el SeÉ ü£L«¢aül©f eNc pw¢nÔø B¢bÑL fË¢aù¡e, Abh¡ S¡j¡eaül©f hÉ¡wL XÊ¡gV, ®f-AX¡l h¡ AÉ ®L¡e fËL¡l eNc¡ue­k¡NÉ ¢h¢e­ju c¢mm (</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Negotiable Instrument</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">) BL¡­l S¡j¡ea ¢qp¡h Bc¡m­a Sj¡c¡e L¢l­a hÉbÑ qC­m, Eš² clM¡Ù¹¢V pl¡p¢l M¡¢lS qC­h, Hhw Bc¡ma I j­jÑ HL¢V B­cn ¢m¢fhÜ L¢l­hz </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 3.25pt 12pt 0.25in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">(6) AbÑ Ge A¡c¡m­a ¢hQl¡d£e ®L¡e j¡jm¡, h¡c£l Ae¤f¢Ù¢Ûal h¡ hÉbÑa¡ ®qa¥ M¡¢lS Ll¡ k¡C­h e¡, Hhw HCl©f ®r­œ Bc¡ma, e¢b­a EfÙÛ¡¢fa L¡NS¡¢c fl£r¡ L¢lu¡ …e¡…e ¢h­nÔo­Z j¡jm¡ ¢eÖf¢š L¢l­hz</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">”</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">From the combined reading of the above provisions, it appears that Artha Rin Adalat Ain, 2003 gives a clear understanding that right after passing of the ex-parte decree or from the date of knowledge of the ex-parte decree if within 30 days as per sub-section (3) of section 19 by depositing 10% of the decreetal amount an application has been filed for restoration of the suit after setting –aside the ex-parte decree, the suit will be automatically restored in terms of section 19(4) of the Ain to its original file and number. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Further, two aspects have been made clear in the said provisions of law that an application for restoration of the suit after setting-aside ex-parte decree may be made within 30 days right after passing of the ex-parte decree or from the date of knowledge of the ex-parte decree. The words used in sub-section 2 of section 19 of Ain “</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">HLalg¡ ¢X¢œ²l a¡¢l­Ml Abh¡ Eš² HLalg¡ ¢X¢œ² pÇf­LÑ AhNa qCh¡l 30 ¢ch­pl j­dÉ, Efd¡l¡ (3) Hl ¢hd¡e p¡­f­r Eš² HL alg¡ ¢XH²£ l­cl SeÉ clM¡Ù¹ L¢l­a f¡¢l­he</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">” clearly indicates two different situations for filing an application for restoration. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Firstly, right after passing of the ex-parte decree and secondly, from the date of knowledge of the ex-parte decree as the case may be. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Now, the question comes to our mind that whether by implication of sub-section 4 of section 19 of the Ain, the suit will be automatically restored in both the situations. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">It is clear from the plain reading of the above provisions of law that right after passing of the ex-parte decree, section 19(4) of the Ain comes into play i.e. the application if so filed within 30 days shall be automatically restored. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">However, it does not apply in a case where it has been contended by the defendant that having knowledge of the ex-parte decree the application for restoration has been filed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Now, it is our view that when the question of knowledge is the basis for deciding an application for restoration that should be decided after taking evidence and hearing both the parties. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Furthermore, it has been decided in the case of Pubali Bank Ltd. vs. Bangladesh and others reported in 66 DLR (HCD) 317 that “Section 19(2) of the Ain does not expressly prescribe for issuance of any notice upon the decree holder to show cause in determining the correctness of the date of knowledge but it is the established principle of law that even when a statute is silent, notice has to be given if any person is sought to be affected in his right, interest, property or character”.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Similar view has been expressed in the Indian Jurisdiction in the Case of Maneka Gandhi vs Union of India reported in AIR 1978(SC)597.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">It is our considered view that after pronouncement of ex-parte decree a legal right has been accrued in favour of the plaintiff (decree holder) and allowing of an application for setting aside the said decree, is curtailing the accrued right of the decree holder. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">In such a situation, our opinion is that the plaintiff has got a right to be informed about hearing of the said application by proper notice and the Adalat after hearing both the parties shall decide the issue as to correctness of the defendants alleged date of knowledge in order to satisfy itself towards the compliance of Section 19(2) of the Ain. In the instant case the Adalat did not comply with the said procedure of law. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Now, in the present case, the ex-parte judgment and decree was passed on 22.03.2009 and as per Section 19(2) of the Ain requires the defendant to file an application for setting aside the ex-parte decree either within 30 days from the date of passing of the said decree or within 30 days from the date of knowledge, about the said ex-parte decree. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Admittedly, it is found from the materials available on record that the respondents were very much aware of the exparte decree dated 22.03.2009 in Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008 as far back as at least in the year 2009 contrary to their claim of date of knowledge that they knew nothing about the suit as well as the decree until 01.01.2012, which is abundantly clear that it is suppression of fact and amounts to fraud upon the court. In the present case, the defendant filed the Miscellaneous Case No. 1 of 2012 on 11.01.2012 which is clearly beyond 30 days of passing the ex-parte decree dated 22.03.2009.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">34.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">It appears from the impugned order dated 16.01.2012 that the learned Judge of the Adalat, only consider one requirement of Section 19 of the Ain of depositing of 10% decreetal amount by the defendant but did not at all consider anything regarding the question of limitation i.e. whether the case is filed within 30 days from the date of knowledge. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">35.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Furthermore, as per Section 3 of the Limitation Act, 1908, which confers a duty upon the Court to see as to whether the suit/application is filed within time or not even if the issue of limitation has not been pressed, the court is legally bound to see and decide such issue in disposing of the matter before it. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">36.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;
