line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Now, the law is well settled that under a Special law where a time limit has been given to file an appeal, the provision of section 5 of limitation Act will not apply and the Artha Rin Adalat Ain 2003, being a special law, the provisions of Section 5 of the limitation Act will not apply and therefore the application for restoration shall be rejected outright. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">37.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Further, ‘he who comes into equity must come with clean hands’. It operates to prevent any affirmative recovery for the person with ‘unclean hands’ no matters how unfairly, the persons adversary has treated him or her. The maxim is the basis of the clean hands doctrine. Its purpose is to protect the integrity of the Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">38.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">In the present facts and circumstances of the case, we hold that the petitioners (respondents herein) of the Miscellaneous Case No. 01 of 2012 have come up with unclean hands. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">39.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">In the Case of Zillur Rahman (Md) vs Md. Abdul Quiyum Sarker reported in 18 BLC(AD) 258 it has been that “Fraud vitiates everything. The plaintiff successed to prove <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">that fraud was practised upon him by the defendant</span> in executing and registering the impugned deed, it vitiated the entire transaction.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">40.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Further it has been held in the case of Janata Insurance Company Ltd vs Commissioner, Customs, Excise and VAT, Dhaka and others reported in 18 BLC (HCD) 562 that “The suppression of fact is a heinous, detestable act, which cuts the very root of any claim made in any discipline, far less to say before Constitutional Court. Therefore, caution goes without any controversy that suppression of fact vitiates everything.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">41.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">It is to be borne in mind that fraud or suppression of fact and fair play cannot dwell together, one must exclude the other. The Court stands for fair play only and to get equitable relief the respondent must approach the Court with clean hands. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">42.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">It is settled legal proposition, decided in the case of United India Insurance Co. Ltd vs. Rajendra Singh and others AIR 2000 SC 1165, wherein the Hon’ble Court observed that “Fraud and Justice never dwell together” and it is a pristine maxim which has never lost its temper over all these centuries.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">43.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">It is our considered view that an act of fraud on Court is always viewed seriously. In judicial proceedings, once fraud is proved, all advantages gained by playing fraud can be taken away. Suppression of any material fact/document amounts to a fraud upon the court.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">44.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">When facts are intentionally misrepresented or where a false statement is made intentionally, with the knowledge that it is false, with a view to deceive the other party, it is known as fraud. In the present case, it is clear that the respondents had knowledge of the ex-parte decree at least in the year of 2009, which is clearly suppression of facts and amounts to committing fraud upon the Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">45.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Further, in the English Jurisdiction, in general, fraud has been defined as ‘Fraud includes the suppression of the truth as well as the presentation of false information.’ Any attempt to deceive is considered fraud, and when the attempt to deceive occurs in a judicial proceeding, it is “fraud upon the Court.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">46.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">From the above discussions, it is crystal clear that the Adalat has committed wrong in passing the impugned order dated 16.01.2012 without deciding the question of limitation, which is a non speaking order and erroneous and should be interfered with as fraud has been committed upon the court. Thus we find merit in the Appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">47.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">In the result, the appeal is allowed without any order as to cost. The impugned order No. 10 dated 16.01.2012 passed by the learned Judge, Artha Ain Adalat, 4<sup>th</sup> Court, Dhaka in Miscellaneous Case No. 01 of 2012 arising out of Artha Rin Suit No. 619 of 2008 is hereby set aside. Consequently, the connected Civil Rule No. 164(F.M) of 2012 is made absolute. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">48.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri;">Communicate the judgment and order to <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the concerned Adalat for taking necessary steps.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 120%; tab-stops: 30.3pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">          Ed.</span></strong></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue_May____19(1)/Issue%20__May__19__F.M.A.%20105%20of%2014__Ahmed%20Sohel__2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">First Miscellaneous Appeal No. 105 of 2012</span></strong></a></p></div></div></div></div>
761	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Abu Bakkar Siddique Vs.  Government of Bangladesh &amp; ors., (Syed Refaat Ahmed, J.)  </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Writ Petition No. 2729 of 2018   </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Syed Refaat Ahmed, J And Md. Iqbal Kabir, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Rokanuddin Mahmud, Senior Advocate with  Mr. Md. Bodruddoza, Advocate  ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Abu Bakkar Siddique and others  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Government of Bangladesh and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Labour Act  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">(SPECIAL ORIGINAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></span></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 209px;" width="499"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 219.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.5pt; font-style: normal;">Syed Refaat Ahmed, J</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">And</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.2pt;">Md. Iqbal Kabir, J</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Judgment on</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">11.02.2019</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 38.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue_May____19(1)/Issue%20_May__19__W.%20P.%202729%20of%2018__Syed%20Refaat%20Ahmed,%20J__6.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 197.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Md. Abu Bakkar Siddique and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . .Petitioners</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Government of Bangladesh and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . .Respondents </span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Labour Act (XLII of 2006)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 3A</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Outsourced employment in the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Airtel Case</em> and the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Khandaker Razib Case </em>leads this Court to find that outsourcing is not a procedural or administrative aberration but is a legally sanctified mainstream mode of hiring. A careful study has been undertaken by this Court of the GTCL Service Regulations, along with amendments thereto and its Schedule, the relevant provisions of the Outsourcing Guidelines, 2008 and the successor Guidelines of 2018 and the set of circulars issued by the Ministry of Finance on 25.8.2013 and 27.1.2016. These rules and regulations collectively convince this Court of the propriety and legality of GTCL’s reliance on the outsourcing mechanism of engaging workers as the Petitioners and their continued employment as such under full legal cover. A proper reading of the Outsourcing Guidelines, 2018 given effect from 1.1.2019, which is read as a consolidating exercise and intended to have a broad base application, leaves no scope for debate or confusion that the Guidelines bring within their ambit the outsourced hired services like drivers. Both on the grounds of maintainability and substantive soundness of the Petitioners’ case this Court, therefore, remains wholly disinclined to a favourable consideration of the Rules Nisi.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>It is noted additionally that this Court’s initial Order of Status Quo was modified by the Appellate Division by its Order of 14.5.2018 enabling the Writ Respondents to follow the usual terms and conditions to deal with the service of the Writ Petitioners henceforth. Given the terms of our findings above and the outcome declared above, we see no discordance with our substantive findings and findings and the effect of the Appellate Division’s Order of 14.5.2018, thereby, enabling GTCL to henceforth continue to engage the Petitioners according to the terms and conditions of service as envisaged in the Outsourcing Agreement already executed between GTCL and Blue-Star Services. That position finds endorsement in practice by Clause 4(C) of the Outsourcing Agreement as previously discussed and indeed Clause 33 of the said Agreement declaring the drivers hired from Blue-Star to be treated as employers of Blue-Star alone with incidences of such employer-employee relationship between </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">Blue-Star and the Petitioners clearly stipulated</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> elsewhere in the said Agreement.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>...(35 to 38)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 109%;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;">Sheikh Abdus Sabur Vs. Returning Officer and others 41 DLR (AD) 1989 Para 29; Kartic Das Gupta Vs. Election Commission of Bangladesh and others 8 ADC 578; Airtel Bangladesh Limited Vs. the Chairman, First Labour Court, Dhaka 19 BLC (2014) 517; Sharmeen Annie Vs. First Labour Court, Dhaka and another, Grameenphone Limited Vs. the Chairman, First Labour Court, Dhaka and Khandaker Razib and others Vs. Government of Bangladesh represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Water Resources and others ref. </span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a name="_Hlk9966321" style="color: #000000;"></a><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Mr. Rokanuddin Mahmud, Senior Advocate with </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Mr. Md. Bodruddoza, Advocate </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">… For the Petitioners </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Mr. Murad Reza, Advocate with</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Mr. Mejbahur Rahman, Advocate</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Ms. Samia Afroz Khan, Advocate</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Ms. Sayeda Silma Tamanina, Advocate and </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Ms. Saida Sharmin Esha, Advocate </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . For the Respondent No.4 </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Ms. Kazi Zinat Hoque, DAG with</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Mr. Shaikat Basu, AAG and</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Ms. Nazma Afreen, AAG</span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>… For the Respondents </span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Syed Refaat Ahmed, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">This Rule Nisi was issued on 25.2.2018 calling upon the Respondents to show cause as to why the failure of the Respondents in causing publication of advertisement in the national dailies for direct recruitment in the post of Driver under the Gas Transmission Company Limited (“GTCL”) should not be declared to be of no legal effect and why the Respondents should not be directed to give priority to the Writ Petitioners in the process of fresh recruitment/appointment in the post of Driver of GTCL relaxing their age limit and/or pass such other or further Order or Orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Well into these proceedings, and at the instance of this Court, the sixty-six Petitioners filed an Application for impleading as Added Respondent No. 13 an entity named Blue-Star Services as operates as an “outsourcing company” in the facts. That Application was allowed on 24.10.2018 given that <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter alia</em> the particular entity Blue-Star Services executed an “Outsourcing Agreement” with GTCL and this Court arrived at the preliminarily satisfaction that its presence as a necessary party in these proceedings would indeed facilitate a more effectual and complete adjudication of all questions and issues in this Writ Petition, thereby, avoiding a multiplicity of proceedings. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-hyphenate: none; tab-stops: 31.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">T</span><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">he Petitioners filed this Writ Petition challenging </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">the failure of GTCL to advertise in the national dailies the direct recruitment of drivers according priority to the Petitioners in the consequential process of fresh recruitment/appointment of drivers under GTCL. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-hyphenate: none; tab-stops: 31.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">GTCL is a subsidiary company of Bangladesh Oil, Gas and Mineral Corporation (hereinafter referred to as “Petrobangla”), and is a hundred percent government owned company. GTCL was registered on 14.12.1993 under the Companies Act, 1913 as a public limited company. GTCL was formed with the objective of establishing a balanced and reliable national gas transmission network with effective and unified control to ensure transportation of required gas for meeting the increasing gas demand in the country. GTCL commenced its formal operation on 23.1.1994 and subsequently started its commercial business from March, 1994.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span></span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-hyphenate: none; tab-stops: 31.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">GTCL, like all other subsidiary companies of Petrobangla, is governed by the provisions of its own employment regulations being the Service Regulations, 1996 (as amended in 2005) as approved by Petrobangla for its subsidiary companies during its 352nd Board Meeting held on 06.06.2005 and later adopted by GTCL.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; mso-hyphenate: none; tab-stops: 31.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">A sheet anchor of the Petitioners’ case is Serial No. 25 of the Schedule of the Service Regulation (the Schedule, itself being amended in 2015). The Schedule specifies the process and qualifications for appointment to listed posts with Serial No. 25, in particular, signifying the post, qualification and experience of drivers, technicians, junior transport supervisers, junior plant operators and similar posts and spelling out the process of such appointments. The Petitioners, however, take issue with and challenge the veracity and authenticity of a perceived appendage to the Schedule identifying “Outsourcing Posts” and enumerating eight posts, inclusive of drivers, whose appointments will be on outsourcing basis. Explained further in this appendage is the fact that as per the 292nd and 317th GTCL Board Meetings held on 28.12.2011 and 19.12.2012 respectively provision has been made on a limited scale in the institutional framework or organogram for <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter alia</em> for only six permanent posts for drivers. The Petitioners consider this entry to be an aberration wholly contradictory to and in negation of the tenor and purport of the entries and listing under Serial No. 25 of the Schedule. They further allege the resort to subterfuge in including the “Outsourcing Posts” list at the very end of the Schedule in a manner as is <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">mala fide</em> and illegal. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 31.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The Respondents for their part allege at this juncture that the Writ Petitioners suppressing this very significant part of the Schedule regarding outsourcing filed the instant Writ Petition. They, accordingly, maintain that GTCL obtained service from the Writ Petitioners wholly in accordance with the provisions of the Service Regulations. Here they draw this Court’s attention to Regulation No. 55(1) of the Service Regulations as states that </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;
