762	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Rabiul Munshi Vs.  Md. Foyez Ahmed Jewel, (Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> First Appeal No. 180 of 2017  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J.  And Sheikh Md. Zakir Hossain, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mrs. Rabeya Bhuiyan, Senior Advocate, with Mr.  Md. Farid Uddin, Advocate, ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Rabiul Munshi and four others </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Foyez Ahmed Jewel and Fourteen others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 265px;" width="556"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 246.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Syed Md. mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-char-type: symbol; Plaintiff-Appellants</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">Md. Foyez Ahmed Jewel and Fourteen others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">. . . Defendant Respondents </span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Section 151</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="color: #000000;">Order VII, Rule 11(d)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The plaint of a suit can be rejected by exercising inherent powers of Court, when from plain reading of the plaint, it appears that the suit is barred under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code.</span> Clause </strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">(d) of the said rule authorise the rejection of a plaint when the suit appears from the statements in the plaint to be barred by any law. This clause applies when it appear</span>s</strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> from the statements in the plaint that the suit is barred but it has no application where there is no clear or specific admission in the plaint suggesting that the suit is barred. This clause is attracted only when on the admitted facts as appearing from the plaint itself the suit is prima facie barred. As for instance when from the statements made in the plaint it appears that the cause of action arose beyond the period of limitation fixed under the statute and no indication is given that limitation has been saved, the plaint may be rejected. In a proper case, when it appears to be barred by limitation, the plaint may be allowed to be amended without rejection. It is not mandatory for the Court to reject the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">pliant.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;"> The </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Court below without considering</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> the materials on record and aforesaid principles of law, by rejecting the plaint of the suit committed an error of law. Therefore, the impugned judgment and decree of the Court below is liable to be interfered by the High Court Division.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span></span><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                       </span>. . . (15, 18 and 29)</strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Mrs. Rabeya Bhuiyan, Senior Advocate,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Md. Farid Uddin, Advocate,</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the plaintiff appellants.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Kamrul Haque Siddiqui, Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Partha Sarathi Mondal, Advocate,</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .For the defendant respondent Nos. 1,3,4 and 15.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">No one appears,</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0.1in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .For the defendant respondent nos. 2 and 5-14.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mrs. Sakila Rowshan, D.A.G. with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mrs. Sharmina Haque, A.A.G.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Kalipada Mridha, A.A.G. and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Mehadi Hasan, A.A.G.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the Proforma defendant respondent nos.16-18.</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 120%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 120%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Syed Md. Ziaul Karim, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">By this appeal,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> the plaintiff appellants have challenged the legality and propriety of the judgment and decree dated 24-04-2017 passed by learned Joint District Judge, Second Court, Comilla, rejecting the plaint of Title Suit no. 34 of 2010 as not being maintainable.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Materials fact leading to this appeal are that on 16-03-2010 the appellants as plaintiffs instituted Title Suit no. 34 of 2010 in the Second Court of Joint District Judge, Comilla impleading the respondents as defendants for declaration that the land described in Schedule ‘Ka’ of the plaint have the easement right of the locality and also for declaration that the deed no. 2158 dated 06-04-2009 in respect of 1.72 acres of land is illegal, void, inoperative and not binding upon the locality. The relieves claimed in the suit reads as hereunder: ‘’</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>“</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">L </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">’</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">ag¢pm h¢ZÑa e¡¢mn£ pÇf¢š­a Aœ ®j¡LŸj¡l h¡c£ frNZ ab¡ Hm¡L¡h¡p£N­Zl CS­j¾V üaÄ ü¡bÑ B­R j­jÑ HL l¡u J ¢XH²£ Aœ h¡c£N­el Ae¤L¥­m J ¢hh¡c£N­Zl fË¢aL¥­m fËQ¡l L¢l­a ;</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>M)<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>BlS£l </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">‘</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">M </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">’</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>N)<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>ju Bc¡ma hÉu¡¢cl ¢XH²£ Aœ h¡c£­cl Ae¤L¥­m ¢hh¡c£N­el fË¢aL¥­m fËc¡e L¢l­a, Hhw </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>O) Bq~e J CL¥C¢V j­a frNZ AeÉ¡eÉ ®k pLm fË¢aL¡l/ EfL¡l f¡Ju¡l qLc¡l ®p j­jÑ B­cn ¢c­a j¢SÑ qu z</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In suit, the plaintiffs filed an application under Order 39 Rules 1 and 2 of the Code of Civil Procedure for restraining the defendant nos. 1-15 from interfering with or causing interference with the public use position, nature and character of the suit land in any way. Defendant nos., 1-4 appeared in the suit and filed written objection against such application denying all the material allegations made in the application for injunction. The application for injunction came up for hearing on 24-04-2017 but the learned Judge of the Court below at the time of disposing of the application for injunction rejected the plaint of suit as barred under estoppel, waiver and acquiescence by the impugned judgment and decree.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Feeling aggrieved by the impugned judgment and decree the plaintiffs as appellants preferred the instant appeal. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate appearing for the appellants seeks to impeach the impugned judgment and decree on three fold arguments:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Firstly:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The question of estoppels, waiver and acquiescence are virtually come within the ambit of principle of resjudicata. It is well settled that the question of resjudicata is mixed question of law and fact and the same are the subject-matter of the evidence which cannot be adjudicated before trial;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Secondly:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The plaint of the suit clearly disclosed the cause of action and from plain reading of the plaint it appears that the same is not at all barred under law. The learned Judge by rejecting the plaint relying on a previously instituted suit which was earlier rejected under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code committed an error of law thereby causing miscarriage of justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Third and lastly:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Even the former Title Suit no.62 of 2000 was rejected under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code but under Order VII Rule 13 of the Code, afresh suit can be entertained. So the impugned judgment and decree cannot be sustained in the eye of law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The learned Advocate appearing for the respondent nos.1, 3, 4 and 15 opposes the appeal and submits that although the instant suit was instituted as a representative capacity by the plaintiffs but no new claim has been asserted in the plaint. He adds that over the self-same matter in issue and schedule land earlier Title Suit no. 62 of 2000 was instituted. It’s plaint was rejected under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code. The plaintiffs or any of the person of the same locality did not seek their redress to any apex Court of law. So the instant suit over the self-same point in issue is barred under law. The learned Counsel lastly submits that the learned Judge of the Court below after considering the materials on record rightly rejected the plaint of the suit by the impugned judgment and decree which calls for no interference by this Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">No one appears on behalf of the respondent nos.2, 5-14 to oppose the appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The learned Deputy Attorney General appearing on behalf of the proforma defendant respondent nos.16-18 opposes the appeal however she submits that the suit land was rightly recorded in the name of the Government and the same is for the public use. So the other defendants have no authority over the suit land.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In order to appreciate their submissions we have gone through the records and given our anxious consideration to their submissions. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The point for consideration whether the impugned judgment and decree calls for interference by this Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">On going to the materials on record it transpires that the plaintiffs in their representative capacity instituted the instant suit for declaration that 1.72 acres of land described in the schedule of the plaint are for public use and the local peoples have the easement right over it and also for declaration that the deed executed in favour of the defendant nos.1-4 is illegal, void, inoperative and not binding upon the peoples of the localities. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The record indicates that in C.S. khatian no.7 of plot no. 31 was recorded as </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">®N¡h¡j</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> and also being used by the locals peoples. It is true that earlier local peoples instituted identical suit being Title Suit no. 62 of 2000 but the same was not decided on merit. The plaint of that suit was rejected under Order VII rule 11 of the Code. In such situation we feel that over the self-same cause of action identical and subsequent suit is not barred under Order VII Rule 13 of the Code. The learned Judge most erroneously relied on the decision dated 01-03-2001 passed in Title Suit no. 62 of 2000 and came to a conclusion that the instant Title Suit no.34 of 2010 is barred by estoppels, waiver and acquiescence. It is pertinent to point out that the aforesaid principles will come within the ambit of principle of <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Resjudicata. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Mahbubul Haque (Md.) vs. Md. A. Kader Munshi 52 DLR(AD) 49 held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-indent: 9pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"> Question of limitation and resjudicata raised in the application for rejecting the point are mixed questions of law and fact which need thorough investigation on adequate evidence for arriving at a correct decision on framing specific issues by the trial Court.”</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">The aforesaid views receives support in the case of Sreemati Pushpa Rani Das vs. AHM Habibur Rahman and others 13 BLD (AD) 217 held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-indent: 9pt; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">“The plea of resjudicata is not available in rejecting a plaint under Order VII Rule 11 C.P.C. This can only be decided on the trial and it cannot be decided from a reading of plaint –resjudicata can be made an issue in the suit.”</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The plaint of a suit can be rejected by exercising inherent powers of Court, when from plain reading of the plaint, it appears that the suit is barred under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; background: white; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: black; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">For the convenience of understanding the provisions of Order VII rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure reads as hereunder:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; background: white; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; color: black; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">″ 11- The plaint shall be rejected on the following issues:</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Where it does not disclose a cause of action.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Where the relief claimed is undervalued, and the plaintiff, on being required by the Court to correct the valuation within a time to be fixed by the Court fails to do so;</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Where the relief claimed is properly valued, but the plaint is written upon paper insufficiently stamped and the plaintiff, on being required by the Court to supply the requisite stamp-paper within a time to be fixed by the Court, fails do so.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><!--[endif]--><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Where the suit appears from the statement in the plaint to be barred by any law.″</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Provided that the time fixed by the Court for the correction of the valuation or supplying of the requisite stamp-paper shall not exceed twenty one days.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">From the plain reading of the statements of plaint of the instant suit it is evident that the same clearly discloses the cause of action; the relief claimed is not undervalued; the plaint was not written upon paper insufficiently stamped; from the statement of the plaint it does not appear that the suit is barred by any law. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now coming to clause (d) of rule 11, it appears that clause (d) of the rule authorise the rejection of a plaint when the suit appears from the statements in the plaint to be barred by any law. This clause applies when it appear from the statements in the plaint that the suit is barred but it has no application where there is no clear or specific admission in the plaint suggesting that the suit is barred. This clause is attracted only when on the admitted facts as appearing from the plaint itself the suit is prima facie barred. As for instance when from the statements made in the plaint it appears that the cause of action arose beyond the period of limitation fixed under the statute and no indication is given that limitation has been saved, the plaint may be rejected. In a proper case, when it appears to be barred by limitation, the plaint may be allowed to be amended without rejection. It is not mandatory for the Court to reject the pliant. It may ask the plaintiff to amend it so as to make suit maintainable. Where the plaintiff does not comply with such an order the Court may reject the plaint. Reference may be made to the cases reported in 18 CWN 1340.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>AIR 1928 Oudh 495 and AIR 1953 Cal.222.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Ratan Chand Dharam Chand Vs. The Secretary of State for India in Council and another, reported in 18 CWN 1340, a Division Bench of Calcutta High Court while considering the scope of Order VII, rule 11(d) observed as follows:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; background: white; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">′′  That rule obviously has no application, for there was no statement in the plaint which suggested that the suit was barred. On the contrary it was specifically stated that notice under sec. 80 had been served on the ′′Collector′′ without specifying the district. The defect was not discovered till after the defendants had entered appearance and it was then too late to reject the plaint ′′. </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Similarly in the case of Maqsood Ali Vs. Deputy Commissioner, Bara Banki and another, reported in A.I.R. 1928, Oudh, 495, a Division Bench of Oudh held that if the suit was not on the face of it barred by any law, Order VII, rule 11(d) had no application. The relevant portion of the judgment ran as follows: </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We do not consider that the suit appeared from the statement in the plaint to be barred by law and we do not think that rule had any application. He has pointed out to us that in a suit which was filed in a similar manner a Bench of the Allahabad High Court stated in Nachhu Vs. Secy. of State that the plaint ought to have been rejected under the proviso of s. 54(c) of the old Code of Civil Procedure, that clause was exactly the same as Order VII rule 11(d). The learned Judge composing the Bench gave no reasons for this conclusion and did not give any effect to it for we find that the suit with which they were concerned had been dismissed but the Subordinate Judge and as their order was an order dismissing the appeal, the plaint was apparently not rejected. Their Lordships said: ′′It ought to have been rejected′′ but gave no effect to that view. We have only to note in respect of this point that exactly the same question could have been raised in Bhagchand Dagadusa Vs. Secy. of State. There the suit had been dismissed by the District Judge. The appeal had been dismissed by the High Court and the appeal was again dismissed by their Lordships of the Judicial Committee. It was not there suggested that the proper procedure was to reject the plaint. In a case such as this we are of opinion that the suit is not on the face of it barred by law. The very arguments which have been advanced in appeal show that the suit on the face of it is not barred by law, as the suit has been found to be a suit that has to be dismissed after consideration of the legal arguments. Therefore we are unable to accept this view of the learned Counsel.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Calcutta High Court in the case of Sreedam Chandra Bhur Vs. Tencori Mukherjee and others reported in A.I.R. 1953 Cal. 222 also held that Order VII rule 11(d) was attracted only when on the admitted facts as appearing from the plaint itself the suit was prima facie barred. The Division Bench in this connection observed as follows:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">′′ This clause is attracted only when on the admitted facts as appearing from the plaint itself the suit is prima facie barred. As for instance when from the statements made in the plaint it appears that the cause of action arose beyond period of limitation fixed under the statute and no indication is given that limitation has been saved, the plaint may be rejected. Even in such a case, an opportunity is to be given to the plaintiff to amend the plaint by setting out an acknowledgement in writing signed by the defendant within the period of limitation if it is so prayed, and that without passing an order for rejection of the plaint. ‘Gunnaji Bhavaji Vs. Makanji<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Khoosal Chand’, 34 Bom. 250. As was observed in ‘Ratan Chand V. Secy. of State 18 Cal. WN 1340, action is to be taken under Or. VII, r. 11 of the Code of civil Procedure only if there is a clear and specific admission in the plaint from which it follows that the suit is barred. Reference may also be made to the observations of this Court.’ Prankrishna Vs, Kripannath’. 21 Cal. WN 209 held:</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">″<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>Let us now consider whether on the plaint as filed the Court will be justified in rejecting in limine the plaint under<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>cl.(d), r.11, Or. VII, Civil P.C.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>In the body of the pliant there is no admission for the Council of the Assembly is the Government under s. 80, Civil P.C. On the other hand, it is seriously contested on behalf of the plaintiff that neither of the two bodies can even be deemed to be the government. The learned Subordinate Judge refers to his order vaguely to the Trend of French Statutes conferring greater and greater powers on the French Settlement in India and creating a ′Council du Government′ there and later a cutting out Chandernagore from the Federation and conferring on Chandernagore all those powers with a separate delegate of the ‘Commissionaire de la re-oblique, it is evident that the Chandernagore administration is a government in the grammatical and ordinary sense of the word though its functions may fall short of the those of the Governments existing in India. </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We do not think it necessary to refer to other points urged before us by the contending parties. Suffice it to say that the question whether even if the Code of Civil Procedure applies, whether s. 80 would be attracted or not cannot be decided merely on the plaint as it stands. The Court should have registered the plaint, issued notices on the defendants and allowed them to file their written statements. After issues were raised it would have been open to the Court to take up one or more of the issues as preliminary ones and decide the same. Objection that had been raised by the Court ‘suo -motu’ and such other objection as may be raised by the defendants would have to be tried on the merits, and only after all the necessary facts and materials are brought before the Court.′′</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">There is no reason to differ from the above principles of law. In the instant case, there is nothing on record to show that on the admitted facts as appearing from the plaint itself the suit is prima facie barred. So the rule 11(d) is not at all attracted here and the plaint cannot be rejected on that score. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Sundar Ali being dead his heirs: Mannan and others Vs. Md. Serajul Islam Sarker and others 56 DLR(AD) 210 held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 22.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">″<em>For the ascertainment of the cause of action the Court is required to read the plaint in its entirety.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Abdul Malek Sawdagar Vs. Md. Mahbubey Alam and others 57 DLR(AD) 18 held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 22.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">″<em> The question whether the plaint is liable to be rejected being barred by law must be apparent from the statement made in the plaint itself and not from the written statement or any other material other than that has been put in the plaint. </em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In the case of Md. Abul Khair Vs. Pubali Bank Ltd. and another 21 BLD (AD)32=53 DLR (AD) 62 held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Where in a suit an application under Order VII Rule 11 of the Code is filed for rejecting the plaint on the ground that the averments made in the plaint do no disclose a cause of action for the suit, the Court is not called upon to decide the suit on merit on taking evidence. It is only the averment made in the plaint which are to be considered to come to a finding as to whether those disclose a cause of action. The Court while deciding such application is not permitted in law to travel beyond the averments made in the plaint. </span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">″</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of Afzal Hossain Diptee Vs. Radha Kanta Korati and others 15 BLC 196 held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-indent: 27pt; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">“Code of Civil Procedure</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-indent: 27pt; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Order VII rule 11</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">On going to materials on record it transpires that the grounds urged for rejection of the plaint are absolutely the subject matter of evidence, which cannot be decided before taking evidence. On plain reading of the statements of the plaint it is evident that the same clearly discloses the cause of action, the relief claimed is not under valued, the plaint was not written upon paper insufficiently stamped and not barred by any other law. The question whether the plaint is liable to be rejected being barred by law must be apparent from the statement made in the plaint itself and not from the written statement or any other material other than that has been put in the plaint.” </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In the case of Bangladesh Water Development Board Vs. Contractor, Manu Barrage 9 BLT 21 held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">“Arbitration Act, 1940</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section -32</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Whether the suit instituted in presence of the arbitration agreement is maintainable.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Held: We find no such provisions in the Act barring a suit on the ground of existence of an arbitration agreement.”</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In the case of Shafi A. Chowdhury Vs. Pubali Bank Ltd. and others 54DLR 310 held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">“<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Section 11 &amp; Order VII rule 11 of the Code.</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Ordinarily, a plaint should not be rejected under Order VII rule 11 of the Code on the ground of res judicata unless it is so palpably clear and obvious from a meaningful reading of the plaint that no further evidence is required.”</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">All the facts and submissions of the learned Counsel for the appellant indicates that the plaint of the suit should not be rejected by exercising the inherent Power of the Court by taking the recourse of Order VII Rule 11 (d) of the Code. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In view of the above, the Court below without considering the materials on record and aforesaid principles of law, by rejecting the plaint of the suit committed an error of law. Therefore, the impugned judgment and decree of the Court below is liable to be interfered by the High Court Division.<span style="mso-tab-count: 2;">                     </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Moreover the impugned order in its entirety is not well founded in the facts and circumstances of the case. So, the submissions advanced by the learned Counsel for the appellants prevails and appears to have a good deal of force. On the contrary the submissions advanced by the learned Counsels for the respondents are not the correct exposition of law and facts. So we are unable to accept their submissions.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In the light of discussions made above and the preponderant judicial view emerging out of the authorities referred to above we are of the view that the impugned judgment and decree suffers from legal infirmities and calls for interference by this Court. Thus the appeal having merit succeeds.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">In view of foregoing narrative, the appeal is allowed. The impugned judgment and decree dated 24</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-04-2017<span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> passed by the learned Joint District Judge, Second Court, Comilla, in Title Suit no. 34 of 2010 is hereby set-aside. The Title Suit no. 34 of 2010 shall proceed in accordance with law.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The office is directed to communicate the order at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue_May____19(1)/Issue%20__May__19__F.A.%20108%20of%2014__Syed%20md.%20Ziaul%20Karim__4.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">F</span></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">irst Appeal No. 180 of 2017</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
763	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Tafikul Islam &amp; ors. Vs.  Government of Bangladesh &amp; ors.,  (Syed Refaat Ahmed, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Writ Petition No. 11886 of 2015  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Syed Refaat Ahmed, J And Md. Salim, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Moudud Ahmed, Senior Advocate with Mr. Probir Neogi, Senior Advocate, Mr. Mohammad Ali Khan, Adv. and Ms. Anita Ghazi Rahman, Advocate  ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2017</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Tarikul Islam and others  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Government of Bangladesh and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Constitutions of Bangladesh </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(SPECIAL ORIGINAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></span></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 199px;" width="423"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 184.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; letter-spacing: -.5pt; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Syed Refaat Ahmed, J</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">And</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Md. Salim, J</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">23.11.2017</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 30.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue_May____19(1)/Issue%20_May__19__W.%20P.%2011886%20of%2015__Syed%20Refaat%20Ahmed,%20J__3.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 164.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Md. Tarikul Islam and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . .Petitioners</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Government of Bangladesh and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US;">. . .Respondents </span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Constitutions of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Article 16</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Is imbibed with a sense of urgent mission single-mindedly pursued rural economic progress. The chosen avenue for such economic upliftment, as informed by the fundamental principle of progress and reduction of disparity underlying article 16 of the Constitution, is not merely the provision of electricity but the collective means of providing the same.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                           </span>. . . (35)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Labour Act (XL of 2006)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 31</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">That the Petitioning have to their detriment ignored a calibration of section 31 within the fabric of the Act itself in favour of instead gauging its validity with standards prevalent under the Act of 2006.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>. . . (36)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Labour Act (XL of 2006)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 31</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">REB (Amendment) Ordinance, 1987</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 23A</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">It is only in that specific limited sense that the reference therein to the Act of 2006 can reasonably merit examination and no more. In other words, the Act of 2006 provides standards to form trade unions in industries-establishments etc. organized on a commercial basis and engaged in activity for profit. The Act through section 31 simply declares that the BREB and PBS are not to be equated with such industries, establish-ments etc. Similar to section 23A introduced under <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">REB (Amendment) Ordinance, 1987,</em> section 31, therefore, is found to have a “tidying up” role in the scheme of the Act. To read anything beyond that into section 31, as indeed the Petitioners have done, as otherwise unreasonably and unjustifiably restricting their guaranteed freedom to form associations and unions is utterly misconceived. Consequently, this Writ Petition, as Mr. Mahbubey Alam has pointed out, reads fundamentally as one pressing the right to form a trade union as contemplated under present labour law legislation. To press such a right through the circuitous route of impugning section 31 is found to be ill-advised if not outright callous and reckless. In that sense, the argument that section 31 is in any way <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ultra vires</em> article 38 is found to be deeply flawed.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                      </span>...(36)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Constitutions of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Articles 16, 38 and 102</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Labour Act (XL of 2006)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 31</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In their arguments of the priority to be given article 38 in determining the vires of section 31 the Petitioner would have been better served in exploring further the essential constitutional link between articles 16 and 38. The constitutional scheme is such that each gives context to the other and cannot, indeed must not, be read to the exclusion of either, especially in a case as this. Any challenge to the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">vires</em> of a statutory provision on the ground that it fails the “reasonable restriction” test must proceed on an “objectivity test” properly identified by any aggrieved person. Any restriction to a guaranteed freedom arising under Part III of the Constitution will invariably have to pass that test. Interestingly, that test seeks to strike a balance between communal good and individual welfare.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                  </span>. . . (37 and 38)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Md. Mehdi Hassan and another Vs. The Government of Bangladesh and others, 1 LCLR [2012] HCD 380; Oali Ahad Vs. Government of Bangladesh 26 DLR (1974), 376 ref.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Moudud Ahmed, Senior Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Probir Neogi, Senior Advocate,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Mohammad Ali Khan, Adv. and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Ms. Anita Ghazi Rahman, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the Petitioners.</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Senior Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Mr. Reja-E-Rabbi Khandoker, Advocate</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> and</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Fazle-Noor Taposh, Advocate</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Ms. Meherunnesa, Advocate</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Saiful Islam, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">… For the Respondent No. 5</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Mr. Murad Reza, Additional Attorney General </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">… For the Respondent No. 1.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoHeading9" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><u><span lang="X-NONE" style="mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Syed Refaat Ahmed, J:-</span></u></strong><span lang="X-NONE" style="mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> In this Application</span><span lang="X-NONE" style="mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> under Article 102 of the Constitution a Rule Nisi was issued calling upon the Respondents to show cause as to why the impugned section 31 of </span><strong><span lang="X-NONE" style="mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">fõ£ ¢hc¤Éa¡ue ®h¡XÑ BCe, 2013 </span></strong><span lang="X-NONE" style="mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(Annexure-A) should not be struck down as the same is unconstitutional and ultra vires to the provision of Article 38 of the Constitution of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh and/or such other or further Order or Orders passed as to this Court may seem fit and proper. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The Petitioners challenge the constitutional</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> validity of section 31 of the </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">fõ£ </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">we`y¨Zvqb †evW© AvBb, 2013 </span></strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Palli Bidyutayan Board Act</span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">2013 </em>(“Act”) (Annexure-A) as published in the Official Gazette on 10.11.2013 repealing the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Rural Electrification Board Ordinance, 1977</em>. This piece of 2013 legislation establishes afresh the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Palli Bidyutayan Board</em> or the Bangladesh Rural Electrification Board (“Board/BREB”) laying out its organizational structure, statutory terms of reference, functions etc. The impugned section 31 of the </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">fõ£ </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">we`y¨Zvqb AvBb,</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;"> 2013</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> Act reads as under: </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">31| †evW©, BZ¨vw`‡K †`vKvb, evwYwR¨K ¯’vcbv, KviLvbv wkí BZ¨vw` wnmv‡e e¨vL¨v bv Kiv| </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">AvcvZZ ejer Ab¨vb¨ †Kvb AvB‡b hvnvB _vKzK bv †Kb kªg AvBb 2006 (2006 m‡bi 42 bs AvBb) Abyhvqx †evW©, mwgwZ ev GB AvB‡b 6 (U) G ewY©Z †Kvb msMVb ev †Kv¤úvbx‡K †`vKvb, evwYwR¨K ¯’vcbv, KviLvbv wkí, evwYwR¨K cÖwZôvb ev wk‡í cÖwZôvb wnmv‡e e¨vLv Kiv hvB‡e bv |</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">It is asserted that workers and labourers working in different societies each styled as <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Palli Bidyut Samity</em> (“PBS”) under the Board/BREB formed an association namely </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">fõ£ </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">we`y¨Z kªwgK Kg©Pvix jxM</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">as per section 176 of the Bangladesh Labour Act, 2006 (Act of 2006) with a view to forging good working relationship amongst its members and a central executive committee was, accordingly, constituted. As per provision of the Act of <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">2006, the Petitioners duly applied for registration</span> as a trade union of the said </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">fõ£ </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">we`y¨r kªwgK Kg©Pvix jxM</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> to the Respondent No. 3, Director of Labour who is also the Registrar of Trade Unions on 10.12.2013. The Respondent No. 3 in his capacity as Registrar of Trade Unions refused vide letter dated 15.12.2013 to register the Petitioners’ trade union by reference to the impugned section 31 of the Act citing the bar thereunder preventing the Board/BREB and societies to be defined as any commercial entity of the likes of a shop, commercial establishment, industry etc.. The implication here being that section 31 operates as a bar, therefore, to the formation of trade unions in the BREB or the societies (</span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">fõ£ </span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">we`y¨r mwgwZ</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">) established to work alongside the BREB. The Petitioners contend that such refusal is tantamount to the workers and labourers of BREB being denied the statutory status of workers as defined under section 2(65) of the Act of 2006.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The spectre of discrimination and inequality of treatment is also<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span>raised by the Petitioners given that workers of several organizations like the Power Development Board (PDB), Dhaka Electric Supply Company Limited (DESCO), Water Development Board, Water Supply and Sewerage Authority (WASA), Public Works Department (PWD), Ashuganj Power Development Company Limited (APDCL),<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>West Zone Power Development Company Limited (DZPDC), Titas Gas Limited etc. are shown to have banded together as registered trade unions.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">It is submitted that because of impugned section 31 of the Act, the workers and labourers working in different societies styled as PBS under the Board/BREB have been arbitrarily ousted from the definition of </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">kªwgK</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> or workers as under section 2(65) of the Act of 2006 and, thereby, deprived of their fundamental freedom to form associations or unions guaranteed under Article 38 of the Constitution In this, the Petitioners see a deliberate and illicit motive behind the formulation of the impugned section 31 to debar BREB workers and labourers working in different societies styled as PBS from forming trade unions.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Bearing in mind, however, that the guarantee under article 38 of the Constitution manifests but a qualified, and not an absolute, freedom to form associations or unions and that such right is “<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">subject to any reasonable restrictions imposed by law in the interests of morality or public order” </em>it is submitted that the Petitioners’ association is not in way related in activity which may be considered subversive or against public interest. The Petitioners, therefore, are unable to find any rational or cogent reason behind enacting the impugned section 31.
