text-align: right;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>. . Petitioner</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The State and another </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="X-NONE" style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Opposite Parties </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Negotiable Instrume</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">nts Act (XXVI of 1881)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 140</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 561A</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the terms as used by the legislature “it is proved” it is clear that mere statement in the petition of complaint, it is not enough to hold a person, responsible of the Company or the other manager, secretary or other officer of the Company, guilty, it needs to be proved by way of evidence. In other wards, so long evidence is </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">not adduced against those persons, they cannot</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">be held guilty. Determination of a person having</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> consent or connivance of, or is attributed to or any negligence on his part during the business of a Company or not is a disputed question of fact and can only be determined upon taking evidence during trial. This question of fact obviously out of the ambit of the Jurisdiction of the High Court Division, conferred under section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure. There is no scope to decide the said question of fact, sitting under Jurisdiction of section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure.” <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                       </span>. . . (12)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">None appears. </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . For the petitioner.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Md. Nasir Shikder, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the Opposite party No.2.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Md. Bashir Ullah, D.A.G.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">…For the State.</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 22.5pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">A.K.M.Asaduzzaman,</span></u></strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> J:</span></u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> This Rule was issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the proceeding of Special Sessions Case No. 53 of 2017 arising out of C.R. Case No.1996 of 2009 (Dakkhin) under section 138 of the Negotiable Instrument Act, 1881, now pending in the Court of Special Sessions Judge, Court No.7, Dhaka should not be quashed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-pagination: none; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt .75in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Facts relevant for disposal of the rule are that the opposite party No.2 as complainant filed a petition of complaint, alleging inter alia, that the accused petitioner availed loan facilities from the complainant opposite party No.2. The accused petitioner’s company failed to adjust his loan liabilities gave cheque to the complainant. Thereafter the complainant deposited the said cheque for encashment but the same were dishonored due to “Insufficient of fund” on 26.01.2009. The complainant sent legal notice to the accused on 02.02.2009 but the accused failed to adjust the same and hence the instant case.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In view of the said petition of complaint, the learned Magistrate took cognizance of the case against the accused petitioner under section 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881 and the case was transmitted to the Court of learned Special Sessions Judge, Court No.7, Dhaka for trial. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The petitioner voluntarily surrendered before the court below and obtained bail and thereafter filed an application under section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure and obtained the instant Rule along with order of stay. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">From reading of the rule petition it appears that the petitioner obtained rule on the ground that there is no averment in the petition of complaint that the petitioner is directly involved in this case even than he has been shown as an accused in the case. The impugned proceeding is thus nothing but an abuse of the process of the Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">None appears for the petitioner although the matter is appearing in the list with the name of the learned advocate for the petitioner.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Heard the learned advocate for the opposite party No.2 and perused the documents annexed to the application.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The learned Advocate appearing for the Opposite party No.2 submits that Sub-section 2 of section 140 of the Negotiable Instrument Act stated that if it is proved that the offence has been committed with the consent or connivance of, or is attributable to, any neglect on the part of any director, manager, secretary or other officer of the company, such director, manager, secretary or other officer shall also be deemed to be guilty of that offence under the Negotiable Instrument Act. In view of the above provision since these contentions are matters of fact and are required to be proved after taking evidence, at the time of trial by the trial court, the rule contains no merit, it may be discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Heard the learned advocate for the opposite party and perused the documents annexed to the application.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The contention as been raised in the rule petition is matter of facts.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Moreover we have already taken a view after analysing the provision of 138 and 140 of the Negotiable Instruments Act that:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>“In the first part of Section 140 of the Negotiable Instruments Act contain the offence committed by the person, who are responsible as well as in charge of the company at the time of commission of offence, shall be deemed to be guilty. But the 2<sup>nd</sup> part of section 140 of the Negotiable Instruments Act provides that any director, manager, secretary or other officer of the company would be held guilty of that offence if at that time they had active part of company as well as consent<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>or connivance of, or is attributable to, any neglect on the part of any director, manager, secretary or other officer of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Moreover in view of the terms as used by the legislature “it is provedˮ it is clear that mere statement in the petition of complaint, it is not enough to held a person, responsible of the Company or the other manager, secretary or other officer of the Company, guilty, it needs to be proved by way of evidence. In other wards, so long evidence is not adduced against those persons, they cannot be held guilty. Determination of a person having consent or connivance of, or is attributed to or any negligence on his part during the business of a Company or not is a disputed question of fact and can only be determined upon taking evidence during trial. This question of fact obviously out of the ambit of the Jurisdiction of the High Court Division, conferred under section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure. There is no scope to decide the said question of fact, sitting under Jurisdiction of section 561A of the Code of Criminal Procedure.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Be that as it may, we find there is nothing to interfere in this Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In the result, the Rule is discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The order of stay granted earlier is hereby recalled and vacated.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Communicate the judgment at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue_May____19(1)/Issue%20__May__19__Crl.%20Misc.%2018246%20of%2018__A.%20K.%20M%20Asaduzzaman,%20J.%20__7.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 18246 of 2018</span></strong></a></p></div></div></div></div>
765	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Uttara Bank Limited Vs. Credit and Commerce Insurance, (Nazmun Ara Sultana, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL APPEAL No. 29 of 2006  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Muzammel Hossain, CJ,  Surendra Kumar Sinha, J,  Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J Nazmun Ara Sultana, J Syed Mahmud Hossain, J, Muhammad Imman Ali, J,  Md. Shamsul Huda, J, </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. N. I. Bhuiyan, Advocate-on-Record.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2012</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Uttara Bank Limited </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Credit and Commerce Insurance (Saudi) Limited and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Constitution of Bangladesh </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-04</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 389px;" width="458"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 199.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Md. padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue_May____19(1)/Issue__May_19__C.%20A.%2029%20of%2006__Nazmun%20Ara%20Sultana,%20J___AD___1.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Uttara Bank Limited</span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . Appellant</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Credit and Commerce Insurance (Saudi) Limited and others </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . .Respondents</span></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Article 103</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Since the defendant-appellant did not raise any question as to the correctness of the concurrent findings of the Courts of facts, rather it has raised a new plea to the effect that the plaintiffs could not prove that the defendant bank sold the said 152 travelers cheques and such new defance plea cannot be raised before the Appellate Division in view of the pleadings of the contesting parties and the evidence adduced by them. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Before this Appellate Division the defendant-</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">appellant did not raise any question as to the correctness of the above concurrent findings of the courts of facts, rather it has raised a new plea to the effect that the plaintiffs could not prove that the defendant bank sold the said 152 travellers’ cheques. But we are unable to accept this new defence plea at this stage specially in view of the pleadings of the contesting parties and the evidence adduced by them. The First National Bank Louisville, Kentucky paid total US$ 77500 against 183 travellers’ chequjles including 148 travellers’ cheques of the disputed transaction. The defendant bank did not try even to controvert the above pleading of the plaintiffs and this exhibit-11 produced by the plaintiffs either before the trial court or before the High Court Division. No suggestion even was ever made to any of the P.Ws. to the effect that the plaintiffs did not pay against those travellers’ cheques or the purchasers did not encash those. The defendant could not return those travellers’ </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">cheques or did not make any statement to the</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> effect that they would return those travelles’ cheques to the plaintiff bank. So, in these circumstances we are unable to accept this new defence plea that the plaintiff could not prove the sale of those travellers’ cheques by the defendant bank. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">       </span>. . . (11)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Appellants :</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Mr. N. I. Bhuiyan,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Advocate-on-Record.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Respondent :</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Mr. Syed Shaheed Hossain, Advocate instructed by Mr. Md. Nawab Ali, Advocate-on-Record.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if supportFields]><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";letter-spacing:-.2pt'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(For the Respondent No. 2-10,</span></b><spanstyle='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";letter-spacing:-.2pt'>(In all the appeals)</span><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";letter-spacing:-.2pt'>) </span></b><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";letter-spacing:-.2pt'><spanstyle='mso-element:field-end'></span></span></b><![endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> Exparte</span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 24pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Nazmun Ara Sultana, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This appeal by leave, at the instance of the defendant Uttara Bank Limited, is directed against the judgment and order dated 03.12.2003 passed by the High Court Division in First Appeal No.235 of 1990 affirming the judgment and decree passed in Money Suit No.1 of 1989 of the 2nd Commercial Court, Dhaka. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The above mentioned Money Suit No.1 of 1989 was filed by the plaintiff-respondents against this defendant-appellant stating, inter-alia, that in the back ground of an agreement dated 27.12.1982 between the plaintiffs and the defendant Uttara Bank Limited the defendant Uttara Bank Limited was to act as an agent and trustee of Bank of Credit and Commerce International (Overseas) Limited (shortly BCCI)- the plaintiff No.2- for sale of BCCI Travellers’ cheques on 14 different terms contained in the letter dated 27.12.1982 (Ext.2). The plaintiff No.1 was the insurer in the transaction to secure the loss of plaintiff No.2. That on 02.04.1984 the defendant bank’s manager Abdus Satter requested to hand over 200 cheques of US$ 500 each to it and BCCI Bank in due course of its business supplied those to Uttara Bank’s authorized cashier Mr. Asgar Ali. Mr. Asgar Ali acknowledged the receipt of 200 travellers’ cheques by signing a trust receipt dated 05.04.1984 (ext.4) as per agreement. Out of 200 those travellers’ cheques Uttara Bank sold 152 cheques to various purchasers and the First National Bank Louisville Kentucky on behalf of BCCI Bank paid US$76000 against those 152 travellers’ cheques to the purchasers in between 30.04.1984 to 21.06.1984. Out of that US$76000 BCCI received payment of US$2000 only vide draft No.003569 dated 31.05.1984. The balance US$74000 not being adjusted BCCI, London by its telex dated 27.09.1984 (Ext.11) addressed to Uttara Bank requested for payment giving detail particulars of travellers’ cheques valued US$74000 paid by its said banker to the various purchasers. That the remaining other 48 travellers’ cheques were not sold by Uttara Bank and those were subsequently recovered from the drawer of Mr. Asgar Ali of Uttara Bank and were returned to BCCI. The defendant bank having not settled the claim, BCCI lodged claim and recovered the value from the insurer (plaintiff No.1) under a letter of subrogation and thereafter BCCI and the insurer jointly filed the suit against Uttara Bank.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The defendant Uttara Bank Limited contested the suit by filing written statement denying the material averments made in the plaint and contending, inter-alia, that the defendant bank never wrote to the plaintiff No.2 to supply travellers’ cheques and did not authorize Mr. Asgar Ali to receive travellers’ cheques on behalf of the defendant, that the requisition letter was not sent by any of the officers of the defendant bank and that the signatures appearing in the requisition letter were not the signature of any of the officers of the defendant bank and this alleged requisition letter was not genuine one and that if any travellers’ cheque was received by Asgar Ali that was received by him in his personal capacity for which the defendant bank was not liable at all.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The trial court decreed the suit on the finding that the plaintiff was able to prove its case that Asgar Ali was authorized by the defendant bank to receive the travellers’ cheques and as such the contention of the defendant bank that Asgar Ali acted beyond the course of his employment in the defendant bank or that the requisition letter was manufactured one was not acceptable. Against that judgment of the trial court the defendant preferred First Appeal No.235 of 1990 before the High Court Division and the High Court Division, after hearing both the parties, dismissed that appeal affirming the judgment and decree of the trial court concurring with the findings of the trial court that the defendant bank’s manager Abdus Sattar wrote the requisition letter to the plaintiff bank to issue travellers’ cheques of US$1,00,000/- for counter sale and that the unsold travellers’ cheques were found in the drawer of Asgar Ali who was in the employment of the defendant bank at the time when the travellers’ cheques were supplied by the plaintiff bank, that from the evidence, both oral and documentary, it was clearly proved that Asgar Ali while in the employment of the defendant bank received travellers’ cheques of US$1,00,000/- and that the defendant did not pay the amount against 148 travellers’ cheques.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Being aggrieved by the judgment and decree of the High Court Division the defendanta-ppellant filed Civil Petition for leave to appeal No.677 of 2004 on the main ground that the plaintiff-respondents failed to prove that the travellers’ cheques were ever encashed or sold by the Uttara Bank and as such it cannot claim sale proceeds of those travellers’ cheques from Uttara Bank.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Leave was granted to consider the submissions of the learned Counsel for the leave petitioner which have been stated in the leave granting order as follows:- </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">“The learned Counsel for the petitioner submits that the High Court Division has committed error of law in not considering that admittedly the transaction between the petitioner and the respondent Nos.2 and 3 being a credit transaction to act as a seller and trustee of the travellers’ cheques of the said respondents and to remit the sale proceeds to the said respondents the petitioner bank is not legally liable to compensate for those travellers’ cheques which were never sold by the petitioner bank.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">He further submits that the High Court Division has committed error of law in not considering that the respondents having failed to prove that the petitioner bank has sold the travellers’ cheques in question, the said respondents cannot claim the sale proceeds of those cheques. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">The learned Counsel for the petitioner lastly submits that the High Court Division has committed error of law in not considering that the respondents having failed to prove that the travellers’ cheques in question were ever enchased, cannot claim proceeds of those cheques from the petitioner bank who acted as a seller and trustee of the traveller cheques.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. N. I. Bhuiyan, the learned advocate-on-record for the appellant has mainly argued before us to the effect that in this case the plaintiff could not prove at all that the travellers’ cheques were ever encashed or sold by Uttara Bank and in the circumstances the plaintiff cannot claim the sale proceeds of those travellers’ cheques from the defendant bank. The learned advocate has argued that there is no evidence on record to prove that the defendant bank sold those travellers’ cheques and in the circumstances the defendant is not legally liable to compensate for those travellers’ cheques which were never sold by the defendant bank. The learned advocate has contended that the High Court Division as well as the trial court committed error of law in not considering that the plaintiff-respondents having failed to prove that the defendant-appellant bank sold the travellers’ cheques in question they cannot claim the sale proceeds of those traveller chaques.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">To controvert the above submission of the learned advocate for the appellant Mr. Syed Shaheed Hossain, the learned advocate for the respondents has pointed out that this plea that the plaintiff could not prove the sale of the traveller’s cheques in question- was not raised or agitated at all by the defendant-appellant either before the trial court or before the High Court Division. The learned advocate has submitted that in those two courts of facts the defendant-appellant pleaded a case to the effect only that the defendant bank or any of its officers never asked the plaintiff bank to issue any travellers’ cheques and that Asgar Ali- the cashier of the defendant bank might have received those travellers’ cheques fradulently in his personal capacity and that for this personal and fraudulent act of Asgar Ali the defendant bank cannot be made responsible for payment for those travellers’ cheques. The learned advocate has pointed out also that both the courts below, on proper consideration of evidence and other materials on record, disbelieved this case of the defendant and accepted the case of the plaintiff that being authorized by the manager of the defendant bank, namely, Abdus Sattar and on the requisition of the said manager Abdus Sattar the cashier Asgar Ali received 200 travellers’ cheques from the plaintiff bank. The learned advocate for the respondents has contended that being defeated in both the courts below the defendant has now made an altogether new case which cannot be considered at all. The learned advocate has submitted further that the plaintiff-respondents stated categorically in their very pleadings that its banker The First National Bank Louisville Kentucky paid the value of 152 travellers’ cheques out of which only US$2000 was reimbursed and the balance was not reimbursed and that in support of this statement the plaintiff’s witness P.W.1 gave oral evidence and produced Ext-11 giving particulars of payment against the balance travellers’ cheques issued by the defendant bank. The learned counsel has pointed out that against these pleadings and evidence of the plaintiffs the defendant did not raise any question either in the trial court or in the appellate court and has argued that in this circumstance the above pleadings and evidence of the plaintiffs are sufficient to prove that those 152 travellers’ cheques were sold. The learned advocate for the respondents has prayed for dismissal of this appeal.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">We have considered the submissions of the learned Advocates of both the sides and gone through the judgment of the courts below and the evidence on record.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It appears that before the trial court and also the appellate court this defendant-appellant denied the claim of the plaintiff by pleading a case to the effect only that in fact the defendant bank or any of its officers never asked the plaintiff bank for issuance of any travellers’ cheques or never sent any requisition for those travellers’ cheques by Asgar Ali, the cashier of the defendant bank and that Asgar Ali might have fraudulently received those travellers’ cheques from the plaintiff bank in his own capacity and not in course of his employment in defendant bank and as such the defendant bank was not responsible for payment of the sale proceeds of those travellers’ cheques. But it appears that both the courts of facts, on meticulous examination of the evidence adduced by both the parties and the facts and circumstances, arrived at the concurrent finding that Abdus Sattar- the manager of the defendant bank sent the requisition (Ext.-3) to the plaintiff bank for issuance of 200 travellers’ cheques and also authorised Asgar Ali the cashier of the defendant bank to receive those <span style="letter-spacing: .1pt;">travellers’ cheques and accordingly Asgar Ali </span></span></span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">received those 200 travellers’ cheques from the plaintiff bank. Before this Appellate Division </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">the defendant-appellant did not raise any question </span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">as to the correctness of the above concurrent findings of the courts of facts, rather it has raised a new plea to the effect that the plaintiffs could not prove that the defendant bank sold </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">the said 152 travellers’ cheques. But we are unable</span><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> to accept this new defence plea at this stage </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">specially in view of the pleadings of the contesting</span><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> parties and the evidence adduced by them.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">11.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It appears that the plaintiffs, in their very plaint, have categorically stated that its banker The First National Bank Louisville Kentucky paid the value of 152 travellers’ cheques in between 30.04.1984 to 21.06.1984 to various purchasers and in support of this statement of the plaint the plaintiff produced exhibit-11- showing particulars of payment against those travellers’ cheques. The exhibit-11 is the Telex dated 27.09.1984 of the BCCI, London, TC Division to Uttara Bank, Dhaka stating in details that The First National Bank Louisville, Kentucky paid total US$ 77500 against 183 travellers’ cheques including 148 travellers’ cheques of the disputed transaction. The defendant bank did not try even to controvert the above pleading of the plaintiffs and this exhibit-11 produced by the plaintiffs either before the trial court or before the High Court Division. No suggestion even was ever made to any of the P.Ws. to the effect that the plaintiffs did not pay against those travellers’ cheques or the purchasers did not encash those. The defendant could not return those travellers’ cheques or did not make any statement to the effect that they would return those travelles’ cheques to the plaintiff bank. So, in these circumstances we are unable to accept this new defence plea that the plaintiff could not prove the sale of those travellers’ cheques by the defendant bank.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times-Roman',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: Times-Roman; mso-bidi-font-family: Times-Roman;">12.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Considering the above facts and circumstances we find no merit in this appeal and hence this appeal is dismissed without any order as to costs.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--></span><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><span style="color: #000000;"> <!--[endif]--> </span><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/Issue_May____19(1)/Issue__May_19__C.%20A.%2029%20of%2006__Nazmun%20Ara%20Sultana,%20J___AD___1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">CIVIL APPEAL No.</span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> 29 of 2006</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(From the judgment and order dated 03.12.2003 passed by the High Court Division in First Appeal No.235 of 1990)</span></span></p></div></div></div></div>
